<p><b>Neil Warnock</b> (born 1 December 1948) is an English <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> <a href="/wiki/Manager_(association_football)" title="Manager (association football)">manager</a> and former player  currently managing <a href="/wiki/EFL_Championship" title="EFL Championship">Championship</a> side <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a>. He is also an established television and radio pundit working for several media outlets and a retired professional footballer. He holds the record for the most promotions in English football, with eight.
</p><p>Warnock played as a <a href="/wiki/Left_winger" class="mw-redirect" title="Left winger">winger</a> for <a href="/wiki/Chesterfield_F.C." title="Chesterfield F.C.">Chesterfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rotherham_United_F.C." title="Rotherham United F.C.">Rotherham United</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hartlepool_United_F.C." title="Hartlepool United F.C.">Hartlepool United</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scunthorpe_United_F.C." title="Scunthorpe United F.C.">Scunthorpe United</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aldershot_F.C." title="Aldershot F.C.">Aldershot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barnsley_F.C." title="Barnsley F.C.">Barnsley</a>, <a href="/wiki/York_City_F.C." title="York City F.C.">York City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crewe_Alexandra_F.C." title="Crewe Alexandra F.C.">Crewe Alexandra</a>, scoring 36 goals in 327 career league appearances. He retired in 1979 at age 30 to move into coaching.
</p><p>Warnock's first managerial job was with non-League <a href="/wiki/Gainsborough_Trinity_F.C." title="Gainsborough Trinity F.C.">Gainsborough Trinity</a> (1980–1981), he would subsequently manage <a href="/wiki/Burton_Albion_F.C." title="Burton Albion F.C.">Burton Albion</a> (1981–1986) and <a href="/wiki/Scarborough_F.C." title="Scarborough F.C.">Scarborough</a> (1986–1989), winning promotion to the <a href="/wiki/Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League">Football League</a> with the latter in 1987. He then managed <a href="/wiki/Notts_County_F.C." title="Notts County F.C.">Notts County</a> (1989–1993), leading them from the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division" title="Football League Third Division">Third Division</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">First Division</a> in successive seasons, though he was sacked after the club were relegated the season before the First Division became the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a>. After a brief spell at <a href="/wiki/Torquay_United_F.C." title="Torquay United F.C.">Torquay United</a> (1993), he moved to <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Town_A.F.C." title="Huddersfield Town A.F.C.">Huddersfield Town</a> (1993–1995), with whom he won promotion to the new First Division. He then resigned and joined <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Argyle_F.C." title="Plymouth Argyle F.C.">Plymouth Argyle</a> (1995–1997), leading them to the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Second_Division" title="Football League Second Division">Second Division</a>. After being sacked, he spent spells with <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Athletic_A.F.C." title="Oldham Athletic A.F.C.">Oldham Athletic</a> (1997–1998) and <a href="/wiki/Bury_F.C." title="Bury F.C.">Bury</a> (1998–1999).
</p><p>In 1999, Warnock joined boyhood club <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United_F.C." title="Sheffield United F.C.">Sheffield United</a>, leading them to the semi-finals of the <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_Football_League_Cup#Semi-finals" title="2002–03 Football League Cup">League Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_FA_Cup#Semi-finals" title="2002–03 FA Cup">FA Cup</a> in 2003 and promotion to the Premier League in 2006. However, he resigned in 2007 after the club were relegated. He then took over at <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_F.C." title="Crystal Palace F.C.">Crystal Palace</a> (2007–2010), saving the club from relegation to <a href="/wiki/Football_League_One" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League One">League One</a>. When the club went into administration, he left to join <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a> (2010–2012), winning promotion to the Premier League with the club in 2011. He was sacked with the club in a precarious position and joined <a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United</a> (2012–2013). After being sacked by Leeds following a poor run of form, he was without a club for almost fifteen months until returning to Crystal Palace, then in the Premier League, in August 2014. In December 2014, he was sacked by Crystal Palace after a poor start to the season, which saw the club in the relegation zone.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCSport_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCSport-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> After a month as caretaker at <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-BBCSportQPR_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCSportQPR-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Warnock returned to Rotherham United as manager in February 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-Rotherham_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rotherham-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> He was appointed manager of Cardiff City in October 2016, and led them to Premier League promotion during the <a href="/wiki/2017-18_EFL_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="2017-18 EFL Championship">2017–18 season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Personal_life"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Personal life</span></a></li>

</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Playing_career">Playing career</span></h2>
<p>After a brief stint working in a local undertakers Warnock started his professional playing career with <a href="/wiki/Chesterfield_F.C." title="Chesterfield F.C.">Chesterfield</a> in 1967, before moving on to <a href="/wiki/Rotherham_United_F.C." title="Rotherham United F.C.">Rotherham United</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hartlepool_United_F.C." title="Hartlepool United F.C.">Hartlepool United</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scunthorpe_United_F.C." title="Scunthorpe United F.C.">Scunthorpe United</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aldershot_F.C." title="Aldershot F.C.">Aldershot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barnsley_F.C." title="Barnsley F.C.">Barnsley</a>, <a href="/wiki/York_City_F.C." title="York City F.C.">York City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crewe_Alexandra_F.C." title="Crewe Alexandra F.C.">Crewe Alexandra</a>, making a total of 327 league appearances in an 11-year playing career. At Hartlepool, he won the club's Player of the Season award in 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> He finished his career at Crewe Alexandra in 1979, aged only 30, to concentrate on training as a coach.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Managerial_career">Managerial career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-League">Non-League</span></h3>
<p>After being involved in Sunday League coaching, his first full managerial job was with <a href="/wiki/Northern_Premier_League" title="Northern Premier League">Northern Premier League</a> side <a href="/wiki/Gainsborough_Trinity_F.C." title="Gainsborough Trinity F.C.">Gainsborough Trinity</a> in 1981. Following this he managed <a href="/wiki/Burton_Albion_F.C." title="Burton Albion F.C.">Burton Albion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scarborough_F.C." title="Scarborough F.C.">Scarborough</a>. At Scarborough he and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Evans_(football_assistant_manager)" class="mw-redirect" title="Paul Evans (football assistant manager)">Paul Evans</a>, his assistant, won the <a href="/wiki/Football_Conference" class="mw-redirect" title="Football Conference">Football Conference</a> title in 1987, making them the first team to win automatic promotion to the <a href="/wiki/Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League">Football League</a> following the abolition of the re-election system.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="With_Mick_Jones">With Mick Jones</span></h3>
<p>Warnock had earlier spent time as a coach at <a href="/wiki/Peterborough_United_F.C." title="Peterborough United F.C.">Peterborough United</a>, where he met Posh assistant boss <a href="/wiki/Mick_Jones_(footballer,_born_1947)" title="Mick Jones (footballer, born 1947)">Mick Jones</a>. In late 1988, Warnock became manager of <a href="/wiki/Notts_County_F.C." title="Notts County F.C.">Notts County</a> – then in the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division" title="Football League Third Division">Third Division</a> – with Jones as his assistant. Also joining the backroom staff were Warnock's assistant at Scarborough, Paul Evans, and ex-Scarborough physio Dave Wilson. The four helped County achieve successive promotions to reach the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">First Division</a> for the <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_in_English_football" title="1991–92 in English football">1991–92 season</a>, with Warnock turning down lucrative offers to manage <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a> during this time.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Warnock, however, was dismissed in January 1993 after County's relegation had cost them a place in the new <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 1993, Warnock took over as "consultant" at <a href="/wiki/Torquay_United_F.C." title="Torquay United F.C.">Torquay United</a>, saving the club from relegation from the Football League. Warnock resumed his partnership with Jones, Evans and Wilson at <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Town_A.F.C." title="Huddersfield Town A.F.C.">Huddersfield Town</a>, his appointment coming in July 1993.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Huddersfield_Town">Huddersfield Town</span></h3>
<p>Warnock was quick to inject new blood into the Terriers' side, snapping up goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Steve_Francis_(footballer)" title="Steve Francis (footballer)">Steve Francis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darren_Bullock" title="Darren Bullock">Darren Bullock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ronnie_Jepson" title="Ronnie Jepson">Ronnie Jepson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Cowan" title="Tom Cowan">Tom Cowan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pat_Scully" title="Pat Scully">Pat Scully</a> during his first season, all of whom would go on to become mainstays in the 1994–95 promotion season. He also showed faith in Centre of Excellence products such as <a href="/wiki/Chris_Billy" title="Chris Billy">Chris Billy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Simon_Baldry" title="Simon Baldry">Simon Baldry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andy_Booth" title="Andy Booth">Andy Booth</a> – a player then struggling to make the breakthrough who would go on to become a club legend in modern times. Despite these acquisitions, Town struggled for most of the 1993–94 season, their last at <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Road" title="Leeds Road">Leeds Road</a>, and Warnock was quick to offload fan favourites <a href="/wiki/Iwan_Roberts" title="Iwan Roberts">Iwan Roberts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iffy_Onoura" class="mw-redirect" title="Iffy Onoura">Iffy Onoura</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Marsden" title="Chris Marsden">Chris Marsden</a> while introducing a more direct style of play. 
</p><p>The run to the <a href="/wiki/1994_Football_League_Trophy_Final" title="1994 Football League Trophy Final">1994 Football League Trophy Final</a> (lost on penalties to <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_A.F.C." title="Swansea City A.F.C.">Swansea City</a>) coincided with an upturn in league form and a mass optimism further bolstered by the move to the new <a href="/wiki/Galpharm_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Galpharm Stadium">Alfred McAlpine Stadium</a> for the 1994–95 season. Warnock's side won the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Electricity_Cup" title="Yorkshire Electricity Cup">Yorkshire Electricity Cup</a> in late 1994. Warnock's side were genuine contenders for automatic promotion until falling away in the final few games to finish 5th (the final play-off spot that season owing to league re-structuring). They triumphed on penalties over second-placed <a href="/wiki/Brentford_F.C." title="Brentford F.C.">Brentford</a> after two thrilling ties and went on to beat <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Rovers_F.C." title="Bristol Rovers F.C.">Bristol Rovers</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a>.
</p><p>He quit Huddersfield just days after their promotion, but made a swift and surprising return to management at <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Argyle_F.C." title="Plymouth Argyle F.C.">Plymouth Argyle</a>, who had just been relegated to Division Three.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plymouth_Argyle">Plymouth Argyle</span></h3>
<p>In his first season as manager of Plymouth Argyle, Warnock took the club to Division Three play-off glory after finishing fourth in the league. The play-off semi-final was a memorable affair – Argyle played Colchester United and were 1–0 down from the first leg, but won 3–1 at Home Park in the second leg. During this game, Warnock was sent off from the dug-out. Warnock responded to this by jumping into the crowd to watch the remainder of the match with the Argyle supporters.
</p><p>The final was the first match that the club had played at Wembley. A header from Ronnie Mauge on 65 minutes gave Argyle a 1–0 win over Darlington and promotion to Division Two.
</p><p>In February 1997, Warnock was surprisingly sacked as Argyle manager despite his popularity with the supporters.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oldham_and_Bury">Oldham and Bury</span></h3>
<p>Following his successful period as manager of Plymouth, Warnock rounded out the 1990s with two relegations, first at <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Athletic_A.F.C." title="Oldham Athletic A.F.C.">Oldham Athletic</a> in the 1996-97 season<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>, and then in 1998-99 at <a href="/wiki/Bury_F.C." title="Bury F.C.">Bury</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sheffield_United">Sheffield United</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Neil_Warnock.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Neil_Warnock.jpg/220px-Neil_Warnock.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/26/Neil_Warnock.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="320" data-file-height="240" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Neil_Warnock.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Warnock with the Blades</div></div></div>
<p>Warnock was appointed as manager of his boyhood club <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United_F.C." title="Sheffield United F.C.">Sheffield United</a> on 2 December 1999. In <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_in_English_football" title="2002–03 in English football">2002–03</a>, Warnock led Sheffield United to the semi-finals of the <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_Football_League_Cup" title="2002–03 Football League Cup">League Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_FA_Cup" title="2002–03 FA Cup">FA Cup</a>, only to lose to <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> respectively, as well as the <a href="/wiki/2003_Football_League_First_Division_playoff_final" class="mw-redirect" title="2003 Football League First Division playoff final">First Division play-off final</a>, with <i>the Blades</i> beaten 3–0 by <a href="/wiki/Wolverhampton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Wolverhampton Wanderers F.C.">Wolverhampton Wanderers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> This was the first time in his management career that he had lost a play-off contest, as he had achieved four promotions via the playoffs in the 1990s.
</p><p>In 2005, Jones resumed the partnership by taking up the assistant's post at <a href="/wiki/Bramall_Lane" title="Bramall Lane">Bramall Lane</a>, and at the end of the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_in_English_football" title="2005–06 in English football">2005–06 season</a>, the club were promoted to the Premier League as runners-up in <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Championship">The Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>The Blades</i> performed well in their expected relegation battle, and for a long time looked to be heading for survival. However, a turning point in the season occurred with victories for both <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a> against <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Athletic_F.C." title="Wigan Athletic F.C.">Wigan Athletic</a>, courtesy of an ex-<i>Blade</i>, on the final day of the season, condemning Warnock's side to relegation. Warnock claimed in his autobiography that minutes after the final game of the season, actor and <i>Blades</i> fan <a href="/wiki/Sean_Bean" title="Sean Bean">Sean Bean</a> burst into his office, blaming Warnock for the team's relegation in a "foul-mouthed tirade" while Warnock's wife and daughter were present. Bean denied this, calling Warnock "bitter" and "hypocritical", and arguing that he would never use such language in front of another man's wife and children. Warnock resigned from the club following relegation to take some time out of football.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A major factor that caused Sheffield United's relegation was that West Ham beat Manchester United on the final day of the season 1–0, with the goal scored by <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Tevez" title="Carlos Tevez">Carlos Tevez</a>, whose contract was in question over third party ownership and who then signed for the champions the very next season. While all of this was happening, <i>the Blades</i> played Wigan at Bramall Lane and needed only one point to stay up; however, with the score at 1–1, a penalty was awarded to Wigan in injury time at the end of the first half – David Unsworth converted. The scoreline remained the same till the final whistle, sending <i>the Blades</i> back to the Championship after only one season.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> There was a slight irony that, earlier on in the season, Unsworth, while playing for Sheffield United, missed a penalty which could have changed the situation at the end of the season.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crystal_Palace">Crystal Palace</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Neil_Warnock_Crystal_Palace.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Neil_Warnock_Crystal_Palace.png/140px-Neil_Warnock_Crystal_Palace.png" decoding="async" width="140" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Neil_Warnock_Crystal_Palace.png/210px-Neil_Warnock_Crystal_Palace.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Neil_Warnock_Crystal_Palace.png/280px-Neil_Warnock_Crystal_Palace.png 2x" data-file-width="604" data-file-height="721" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Neil_Warnock_Crystal_Palace.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Warnock with Palace</div></div></div>
<p>Warnock spoke to <a href="/wiki/Milan_Mandari%C4%87" title="Milan Mandarić">Milan Mandarić</a> about the vacant managerial role at <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a> in the summer, but was never handed the job.<sup id="cite_ref-Made_in_Sheffield:_Neil_Warnock_-_My_Story_343-344_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Made_in_Sheffield:_Neil_Warnock_-_My_Story_343-344-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Simon_Jordan" title="Simon Jordan">Simon Jordan</a> spoke to Warnock about taking over at <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_F.C." title="Crystal Palace F.C.">Crystal Palace</a> following the sacking of <a href="/wiki/Peter_Taylor_(footballer,_born_1953)" title="Peter Taylor (footballer, born 1953)">Peter Taylor</a> and, after initially not being keen over the job, he returned to football management with Palace on 11 October 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-Made_in_Sheffield:_Neil_Warnock_-_My_Story_346_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Made_in_Sheffield:_Neil_Warnock_-_My_Story_346-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Warnock_appointed_as_Palace_boss_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Warnock_appointed_as_Palace_boss-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Having his personal friend <a href="/wiki/Simon_Jordan" title="Simon Jordan">Simon Jordan</a> as owner and chairman was certainly a help in him getting the job. Jones returned from his own sabbatical to join Warnock's team as assistant. Under Warnock and Jones, Palace made a massive turn-around, moving from relegation battlers to promotion contenders in the space of six months, with Warnock's use of youngsters a major factor in the improved performances and results. Palace made the play-offs in the end, but were beaten at the semi-final stage by <a href="/wiki/Bristol_City_F.C." title="Bristol City F.C.">Bristol City</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> who went on to lose to <a href="/wiki/Hull_City_A.F.C." title="Hull City A.F.C.">Hull City</a> in the final.
</p><p>Warnock stayed on for the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_in_English_football" title="2008–09 in English football">2008–09 season</a>, but on taking the job a year earlier he had made it clear that the Crystal Palace job would be his last managerial role in football, with the club's finances beginning to take a turn for the worse. The <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_in_English_football" title="2009–10 in English football">2009–10 season</a> saw Palace perform well despite being heavily restricted by the club's poor financial position, which resulted in the club being placed in administration late in January. A ten-point deduction was imposed by the Football League for this.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Crystal Palace's administrator commented that Warnock was "let go" after telling the administrator he did not have the stomach for the fight to save the club.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Queens_Park_Rangers">Queens Park Rangers</span></h3>
<p>On 1 March 2010, Warnock joined <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a> as manager on a three-and-a-half-year deal after agreeing compensation with Crystal Palace.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> His first match in charge was an emphatic 3–1 home win against <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Bromwich Albion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He helped QPR comfortably avoid relegation in 2009–10 – including a 2–0 win against former club Crystal Palace at <a href="/wiki/Selhurst_Park" title="Selhurst Park">Selhurst Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Warnock was awarded Manager of the Month for August 2010. Using a new 4–2–3–1 formation built around playmaker <a href="/wiki/Adel_Taarabt" title="Adel Taarabt">Adel Taarabt</a> (who went on to win the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Championship">Football League Championship</a> Player of the Year 2011), QPR topped the table for the majority of the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Football_League_Championship" title="2010–11 Football League Championship">2010–11 season</a> and on 30 April 2011 were promoted as <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Championship">Championship</a> champions after a 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite leading the club to the Premier League for the first time in 15 years, he was sacked on 8 January 2012 after the 1–2 home defeat to <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_F.C." title="Norwich City F.C.">Norwich City</a> on 2 January 2012. The owner of QPR, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Fernandes" title="Tony Fernandes">Tony Fernandes</a>, said that the club slipped down to a dangerous league position (17th) after recent results.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Warnock said, "Obviously I'm very disappointed but, having achieved so much, I leave the club with a great sense of pride. I have enjoyed my time here more than anywhere else and the QPR fans have been brilliant with me – they deserve success. My biggest regret is that the takeover didn't happen earlier, because that would have given me the opportunity to bring in the targets I'd pinpointed all last summer and probably given us a better chance to succeed in the Premier League. The board at QPR are hugely ambitious and I wish them every success for the future. I've been involved in the game a long time and I will be spending the immediate future with my family and friends before deciding my next career move."<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leeds_United">Leeds United</span></h3>
<p>On 18 February 2012, Warnock joined Leeds as manager on a one-and-a-half-year deal taking him up to the end of the 2012–13 season.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Before officially taking charge from caretaker manager <a href="/wiki/Neil_Redfearn" title="Neil Redfearn">Neil Redfearn</a> he oversaw Leeds win 3–2 against <a href="/wiki/Doncaster_Rovers_F.C." title="Doncaster Rovers F.C.">Doncaster Rovers</a> from the stands on 18 February with Warnock revealing he spoke to the players before the game and at half-time.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> On 28 February 2012, Warnock made his first signing as Leeds manager by bringing in <a href="/wiki/Danny_Webber" title="Danny Webber">Danny Webber</a>, whom he managed while at Sheffield United.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Leeds would go on to finish 14th in the Championship and during the summer of 2012 Warnock revamped the entire Leeds team with several new signings. Warnock started the 2012–13 season with a home win in the League Cup beating <a href="/wiki/Shrewsbury_Town_F.C." title="Shrewsbury Town F.C.">Shrewsbury Town</a> 4–0.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Leeds would then go on to beat Wolves 1–0 at Elland Road on the opening day of the Championship.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>After a string of defeats and Leeds sitting five points off the relegation zone, Warnock parted company with the club on 1 April 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_Crystal_Palace">Return to Crystal Palace</span></h3>
<p>On 27 August 2014, it was announced that Warnock would be appointed for a second spell in charge at Crystal Palace following the departure of <a href="/wiki/Tony_Pulis" title="Tony Pulis">Tony Pulis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> However, after a poor run of form, and Crystal Palace ending up in the bottom three, Warnock was sacked by the club on 27 December 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCSport_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCSport-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> He was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Alan_Pardew" title="Alan Pardew">Alan Pardew</a> on 2 January 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_Queens_Park_Rangers">Return to Queens Park Rangers</span></h3>
<p>In 2015, Warnock returned to Queens Park Rangers as first team advisor. On 4 November, he was placed in temporary charge of QPR following the departure of Chris Ramsey from the club.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rotherham_United">Rotherham United</span></h3>
<p>On 11 February 2016, Neil Warnock was confirmed as the new <a href="/wiki/Rotherham_United_F.C." title="Rotherham United F.C.">Rotherham United</a> manager for the remainder of the 2015–16 season, replacing <a href="/wiki/Neil_Redfearn" title="Neil Redfearn">Neil Redfearn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rotherham_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rotherham-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Warnock drew his first game in charge with a 0–0 draw against <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_City_F.C." title="Birmingham City F.C.">Birmingham City</a> in a match which saw both <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wood_(footballer)" title="Richard Wood (footballer)">Richard Wood</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Mattock" title="Joe Mattock">Joe Mattock</a> sent off. He then lost his next two games, against <a href="/wiki/Reading_F.C." title="Reading F.C.">Reading</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burnley_F.C." title="Burnley F.C.">Burnley</a>, 2–0. Rotherham then went on an unbeaten run of 11 matches, including wins against Brentford (2–1), Sheffield Wednesday (1–0), <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough</a> (1–0), drawing against <a href="/wiki/Derby_County_F.C." title="Derby County F.C.">Derby County</a> 3–3 after being 3–0 down with eight minutes to go, and winning 1–0 at <a href="/wiki/Portman_Road" title="Portman Road">Portman Road</a> against <a href="/wiki/Ipswich_Town_F.C." title="Ipswich Town F.C.">Ipswich Town</a>. Warnock was awarded the Championship Manager of the Month for March. The final win of the run was at <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Dons_F.C." title="Milton Keynes Dons F.C.">Milton Keynes Dons</a>, where a 4–0 thrashing all but sealed Rotherham's survival in the Championship at the expense of their opponents. The season closed with Warnock stating he wanted one last season managing in the Championship and Rotherham hoping to secure his services for 2016–17.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cardiff_City">Cardiff City</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cardiff_City_celebrations_2018.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Cardiff_City_celebrations_2018.jpg/220px-Cardiff_City_celebrations_2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Cardiff_City_celebrations_2018.jpg/330px-Cardiff_City_celebrations_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Cardiff_City_celebrations_2018.jpg/440px-Cardiff_City_celebrations_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3888" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cardiff_City_celebrations_2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Warnock (holding trophy right) lifts the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_EFL_Championship" title="2017–18 EFL Championship">2017–18 EFL Championship</a> runner-up trophy with <a href="/wiki/Sean_Morrison_(footballer)" title="Sean Morrison (footballer)">Sean Morrison</a></div></div></div>
<p>On 5 October 2016, Warnock was appointed first team manager of <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> They finished in 12th place in the <a href="/wiki/EFL_Championship" title="EFL Championship">Championship</a> in Warnock's first season in charge.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> On 6 May 2018, Warnock guided Cardiff to promotion to the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> after a 0–0 draw against <a href="/wiki/Reading_F.C." title="Reading F.C.">Reading</a>. With this promotion Warnock became the first manager to win eight promotions in the professional leagues.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> However, he was unable to keep the team up and the team were relegated back to the Championship at the end of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>Warnock was born in <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a>, West Riding of Yorkshire.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> He has been a lifelong supporter of Sheffield United. He is married to Sharon and has four children, James, Natalie, Amy and William.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neil_Warnock&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, he lived in <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_London" title="Richmond, London">Richmond</a>, London<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> and had a home in <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Warnock is in favour of <a href="/wiki/Britain_leaving_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Britain leaving the European Union">Britain leaving the European Union</a>. In a press conference after a Cardiff City game in January 2019, he remarked that: “I can’t wait to get out of it, if I’m honest. I think we’ll be far better out of the bloody thing. In every aspect. Football-wise as well, absolutely. To hell with the rest of the world."<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
